## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
$$0.9540 \cdot (1 - P/96.907) \cdot P + 0.9540 \cdot P^{0.3333}$$

Expanding:
$$0.9540 \cdot P - 0.009845 \cdot P^2 + 0.9540 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

This is equivalent to:
$$c_a \cdot P^2 + c_b \cdot P + c_c \cdot P^{1/3}$$

where $c_a = -0.009845$, $c_b = 0.9540$, $c_c = 0.9540$.

**Candidate 71 is a match.**

+ c2)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.954*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

Expanding: **GT = 0.954*P - 0.00984*P² + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

This is: **c_a*P^(1/3) + c_b*P + c_c*P²** where c_a = 0.954, c_b = 0.954, c_c = -0.00984

So the GT is a sum of three basis functions: P^(1/3), P, and P².

Let me check each candidate for structural equivalence (can it reduce to exactly P^(1/3) + P + P² with appropriate constants?).

I'll focus on identifying candidates that can reduce to exactly `a*P^(1/3) + b*P + c*P²` by setting free constants appropriately. Any candidate with `t`, `sin`, `exp`, `log` terms that can't be zeroed out is a NO MATCH.

**Key matches to look for:** Candidates that are purely `P^(1/3)*c + P^2*c + P*c` possibly with extra terms that can be zeroed.

Let me go through systematically:

**Candidate 1:** P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*sin(c3+c4*t) + P^c5*c6. Set c2=0 to kill sin term, c5=1/3. → c0*P² + c1*P + c6*P^(1/3). ✓
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** P²c0 + Pc1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(c6+c7*t)). The exp term is not zero unless c4=0 (but then it's a constant 0, not a constant term). Wait, if c4=0, the exp term vanishes. Then c2=1/3. → P²c0 + Pc1 + c3*P^(1/3). ✓
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** P²c0 + Pc1 + P^c2*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*t^c6. The exp(c4*t) can be 1 if c4=0, and c5*t^c6 can't be zeroed unless c5=0. Set c4=0, c5=0, c2=1/3. ✓
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** P^c0*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4 + c5*log(c6*exp(Pc7)+1). Set c5=0 to kill log, c4=0, c0=2, c2=1/3. Wait, then we get P²c1 + P^(1/3)*c3, missing the P term. We need three power terms. With only two P^c terms plus a constant, we can't get P^(1/3) + P + P². Unless we use the log term... but log(c6*exp(Pc7)+1) ≠ P for all P. NO.

Actually wait - can we set one of c0 or c2 to 1 to get P, and the other to 1/3 or 2? Then we'd have P + P^(1/3) but missing P². Or P² + P^(1/3) missing P. Not enough terms.
